  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a92339a0-5e85-4fc6-a2cc-1f48f41354ab'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497649448" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497649448?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497649448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5413124180284136618">Surprisingly, I was able to wholly like Celaena in this one. I have some sort of love/hate relationship with her but she actually kept her arrogance at a bare minimum in this story which I'm grateful for. Celaena's/Aelin's arrogance can be quite suffocating so it's actually a relief to see a "normal" side to her without her spewing some smartass comment every other page.<br/><br/>Yrene was a pretty interesting character! I would want to see more of her and more of the healers in this world. Maybe we'll se</span>
  <span id="freeText5413124180284136618" style="display:none">Surprisingly, I was able to wholly like Celaena in this one. I have some sort of love/hate relationship with her but she actually kept her arrogance at a bare minimum in this story which I'm grateful for. Celaena's/Aelin's arrogance can be quite suffocating so it's actually a relief to see a "normal" side to her without her spewing some smartass comment every other page.<br /><br />Yrene was a pretty interesting character! I would want to see more of her and more of the healers in this world. Maybe we'll see a bit of Antica in Empire of Storms? Maybe we'll see Yrene again? Because you know who is going to Antica to you know what... Maybe. :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15648574571008244021"><u>3 STAR'S</u> <br/><br/><i>“The girl wore her scars the way some women wore their finest jewelry.”</i><br/><br/>In this novella of <i>The Assassin and the Healer</i>, it was better than I thought it was gonna be. Again for the first half, it was really slow and dragged a bit. But the last half got a lot better and more interesting. I loved getting to see Yrene before she became the badass healer she is in <i>Tower of Dawn</i>. She is such a sweet, kind and all-around wonderful character :) I am looking so forward to seeing more of her in <i>Ki</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15648574571008244021" style="display:none"><u>3 STAR'S</u> <br><br><i>“The girl wore her scars the way some women wore their finest jewelry.”</i><br><br>In this novella of <i>The Assassin and the Healer</i>, it was better than I thought it was gonna be. Again for the first half, it was really slow and dragged a bit. But the last half got a lot better and more interesting. I loved getting to see Yrene before she became the badass healer she is in <i>Tower of Dawn</i>. She is such a sweet, kind and all-around wonderful character :) I am looking so forward to seeing more of her in <i>Kingdom of Ash</i>!! I also always enjoy seeing Celaena help out those who are in need of it. I have always loved Celaena and that love was no different in this one. I for one love Celaena more and more with each passing book and have excepted her and all the flaws that come with her character. One of my favorite parts was when Celaena was teaching Yrene how to defend herself. But really it didn't add many contexts to the story as a whole. Moving on to <i>The Assassin and the Desert</i>. I'm excited about this one!! :D<br><br><i>“The girl was alluring. Like wildfire, or a summer storm swept off the Gulf of Oro.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1536537245ra/26279671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18364868544214565200"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>So after ruining her master's slavery trade deal with the pirate lord in the previous novella, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2672223318' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE ASSASSIN AND THE PIRATE LORD</a>, Celery is sent on a punishment mission to the Bumfuck Desert, or whatever it's called, where she is about as subtle and professional as you would expect (i.e. not at all). She wears a hooded cloak and flashes her weapons while hanging around in this inn like a total creep, and of course, <i>everyone </i>in the place i</span>
  <span id="freeText18364868544214565200" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>So after ruining her master's slavery trade deal with the pirate lord in the previous novella, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2672223318" rel="nofollow noopener">THE ASSASSIN AND THE PIRATE LORD</a>, Celery is sent on a punishment mission to the Bumfuck Desert, or whatever it's called, where she is about as subtle and professional as you would expect (i.e. not at all). She wears a hooded cloak and flashes her weapons while hanging around in this inn like a total creep, and of course, <i>everyone </i>in the place is completely fixated on her, wondering who dis?<br><br><br><br>The other main character is Yrene, who ends up becoming Chaol's wife later on in the series. She's a barmaid in this one, having resigned herself to the fantasy world equivalent of working in a McDonald's after she found she was too poor to go to healer school. She wears a wedding ring to fake out creepers and is generally totally miserable. This new cowled assassin is the most excitement she's ever gotten in her sad little life.<br><br><br><br>Naturally, Celery saves Yrene from mercenaries and naturally, Yrene can't stop fangirling over the awesomeness that is Celery, whether it's her amazing gold-rimmed blue eyes or the fact that she's <i>so tough omg</i>, or the fact that she has a veritable Derek Zoolander catalog of ~lewks~ ranging from "roguish grin" to "wild grin."<br><br><br><br>The book ends with Celery strutting off like she is the best thing since the internet, leaving behind a bag of money for Yrene to go off and stake her fortune. Presumably, Celery was indirectly the reason that Yrene even met Chaol in the first place and was able to heal him, which I guess is supposed to make me love Celery even more. #NiceTryButNope<br><br><br><br>So far these novellas are feeling an awful lot like self-fanfiction. They don't really add anything to the main story and mostly just kiss Celaena's pale little ass. As if it needed more kissing.<br><br><br><br>1 star</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12792223210379968767">I love this novella that is more likely a short story. Despite being a heartless assassin, <b>Celaena Sardothien</b> surprised me once again with the way she influenced the characters that surround her. This part of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b> book takes place in the land called <i>Innish</i> where Celaena met the gifted healer <b>Yrene Towers</b>. Yrene was a lot more different because she grew up weak-willed compared to the headstrong Celaena. But then, Celaena made a difference to Yrene when she helped her and basically</span>
  <span id="freeText12792223210379968767" style="display:none">I love this novella that is more likely a short story. Despite being a heartless assassin, <b>Celaena Sardothien</b> surprised me once again with the way she influenced the characters that surround her. This part of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b> book takes place in the land called <i>Innish</i> where Celaena met the gifted healer <b>Yrene Towers</b>. Yrene was a lot more different because she grew up weak-willed compared to the headstrong Celaena. But then, Celaena made a difference to Yrene when she helped her and basically taught her how to fight and to be determined to follow the path she wants to take. This short story tugged my heart. It also made me wonder if Yrene really followed Celaena’s advice.<br /><br />Rating: 4 Stars</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25978565-the-assassin-and-the-healer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=physical-shelf">physical-shelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780746239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14280813979895166619">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br/><br/>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin'</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14280813979895166619" style="display:none">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br /><br />I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin's Blade</b>. And because I love <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J_Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas's</a>
</b> story telling and her writing, I am going to go ahead and read these beauties.<br /><br />So, with that said, I am going to read and rate these so I can finally be completely caught up on The Throne of Glass Series: Throne of Glass, Crown of Midnight, Heir of Fire, Queen of Shadows, Empire of Storms, and Tower of Dawn.<br /><br /><u>The Assassin and the Healer (Throne of Glass, #0.2)</u><br />This story was less interesting than The Assassin and the Pirate Lord. <br /><br />I will say this though: You do see Celaena having a softer side to herself. She sees this healer as helpless and pathetic, but when she realizes she could actually benefit from a thing here and there and could make a difference for someone in return... well, let's just say she may help but not in the way that is expected of her. She's a little rough around the edges to say the least.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer893210618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4910518458987158535"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Ugh, Celaena was such a disgusting, stuck up, stupid cow in this. I usually like her arrogant, opinionated attitude (it's a refreshing change from the usual oh so modest goody-goody heroine) but it really irritated this time around. When the giddy cow saved a young barmaid (Yrene) from being attacked by four men the douche blamed Yrene for them going after her. The victim blaming attitude really pissed me off, apparently Yrene had the attack coming because she deigned to go outside and t</span>
  <span id="freeText4910518458987158535" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Ugh, Celaena was such a disgusting, stuck up, stupid cow in this. I usually like her arrogant, opinionated attitude (it's a refreshing change from the usual oh so modest goody-goody heroine) but it really irritated this time around. When the giddy cow saved a young barmaid (Yrene) from being attacked by four men the douche blamed Yrene for them going after her. The victim blaming attitude really pissed me off, apparently Yrene had the attack coming because she deigned to go outside and throw the rubbish out at the end of her shift. So in Celaena's mind Yrene simply doing the job that she was paid to do and that kept a roof over her head was Yrene actually being dumb and asking for trouble. That's a great message — don't work or go outside otherwise it's your fault for being attacked. Ugh, Celaena was beyond hideous.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4910518458987158535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1385704307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer291879015164582917">This novella reminded me why I couldn't finish <i>Heir of Fire</i>, SJM has a habit of introducing many new characters that we have yet to care about and shove them down our throats. Instead of easing us into their world. <br/><br/>I was waiting for something to happen, anything! But no, this novella was just a reminder of how perfect Celeana is from the healer's POV. And after a few hundred times, it gets boring. <br/><br/>The extra star is for the ending which picked up a bit, but not enough to redeem this novella.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1884912979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1884912979" />
    <a title="_racheljane_" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54315548-racheljane"><img alt="_racheljane_" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469002514p2/54315548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884912979?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="_racheljane_" class="user" itemprop="url" name="_racheljane_" href="/user/show/54315548-racheljane">_racheljane_</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884912979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12797372633497670280">This novella is different from the first one. Most of the story is told from Yrene’s perspective, which I like a lot. We get to see Celaena from someone else’s point of view. Yrene and Celaena are two completely different people. Celaena is a ruthless assassin and Yrene is a barmaid who can’t fight for herself. I think that Celaena helps Yrene because she wants to make the world a better place. We got a glimpse of this in the first novella as well.<br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

Because of Celaena's actions in  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745677521" rel="nofollow noopener">The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</a>, she is sent away on a punishment mission. While waiting for a boat to take her to her punishment, she is staying at the White Pig Inn, where she meets a very unique and kindhearted girl named Yrene. <br /><br />I really liked Yrene, and the little bit of her back-story that we received, but this novella just completely felt like filler for me. Maybe we will see Yrene in this series eventually, and then this story will be a lot more meaningful, but as it stands, this story felt the weakest in this bind-up.<br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>

<div id="review_1282079557" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1282079557" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1282079557?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who wants to see the kind parts of an assassin.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=great-fighting-scenes">great-fighting-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282079557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6299587973070862655"><p>It was actually an interesting combination, considering that the <i>assassin</i> and the <i>healer</i> are two opposite sides of a coin and they helped each other. Much to my relief, there was a small part of Celaena Sardothien that wanted to make the world a better place, despite the fact that she was the most notorious and also the best protégée of Arobynn, the King of Assassins's, apprentices.</p><br/><p>In short, it's a novella without too many bloody fight scenes(of course, beating bad guys didn't count!) and Celaen</p></span>
  <span id="freeText6299587973070862655" style="display:none"><p>It was actually an interesting combination, considering that the <i>assassin</i> and the <i>healer</i> are two opposite sides of a coin and they helped each other. Much to my relief, there was a small part of Celaena Sardothien that wanted to make the world a better place, despite the fact that she was the most notorious and also the best protégée of Arobynn, the King of Assassins's, apprentices.</p><br /><p>In short, it's a novella without too many bloody fight scenes(of course, beating bad guys didn't count!) and Celaena proved that deep inside her heart lied a slice of mercy, friendliness, and most important of all, love.<br /><b><blockquote>"For wherever you need to go---and then some. The world needs more healers.</blockquote></b><br /></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="6299587973070862655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer850541799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2270407123702225741">This is not really a novella, I would call this a short story that takes place between novella 0.1 and 0.2.<br/><br/>Unlike novellas 0.1-0.4, which are essential to the story and need to be read, this one is not essential, and you could skip it if you wanted. Basically, if you've finished them all but aren't ready to let go of these characters, then yeah... go ahead. The good thing is that this one is free, and I'll mention where to find it in a second because <i>THAT</i> was a major hunt for me.<br/><br/>This story takes</span>
  <span id="freeText2270407123702225741" style="display:none">This is not really a novella, I would call this a short story that takes place between novella 0.1 and 0.2.<br /><br />Unlike novellas 0.1-0.4, which are essential to the story and need to be read, this one is not essential, and you could skip it if you wanted. Basically, if you've finished them all but aren't ready to let go of these characters, then yeah... go ahead. The good thing is that this one is free, and I'll mention where to find it in a second because <i>THAT</i> was a major hunt for me.<br /><br />This story takes place when Celaena is on her journey to the Red Desert. She stops at an inn/tavern along the way and meets a barmaid. We get an outside impression of Celaena because half of the story is told through the barmaid's eyes (It's third person like the rest of the books still), and then Celaena and the girl end up spending one night together after Celaena saves her from an attack, and Celaena learns more about the girl's story.<br /><br />Now, for where to find this one. Two options. You can buy the 0.1-0.5 kindle bundle or paperback (it is included in that book, its title is <i>The Assassin's Blade</i>), <b>OR</b> you can read it here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.movellas.com/mobile/app/read.htm?movellaId=201301311152267426">http://www.movellas.com/mobile/app/re...</a><br /><br />And I was able to read that link right on my phone.<br /><br />It was well written, but it's just a frivolous side story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2270407123702225741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2qMLe5GS7rIzJG/c9zK9umheHeJkK3wPRjvGOSNa2FwNBs4z+D6MO0MG1kIFxDDgaAOSjBgjqRFs3SIq0ngQBA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6sb4IAy9IRomROnakgE7bRW61hBLFkHdgMWMGwmPEDg9Yz1oZRFDk1ZmUERg97Y3FedZfjcelMOqI2gI+K3YYA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer12629579555486614327">Sarah J. Maas is the #1 New York Times and internationally bestselling author of the Crescent City, A Court of Thorns and Roses, and the Throne of Glass series. Her books have sold more than twelve million copies and are published in thirty-seven languages. A New York native, Sarah lives in Philadelphia with her husband, son, and dog. To find out more, visit sarahjmaas.com or follow @therealsjmaas</span>
  <span id="freeText12629579555486614327" style="display:none">Sarah J. Her books have sold more than twelve million copies and are published in thirty-seven languages. A New York native, Sarah lives in Philadelphia with her husband, son, and dog.
